<p><b>Miami-Dade County</b> (formerly <b>Dade County</b>) is an American <a href="/wiki/County_(United_States)" title="County (United States)">county</a> located in the southeastern part of the <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">U.S. state</a> of <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a>. It is the southeasternmost county on the <a href="/wiki/Contiguous_United_States" title="Contiguous United States">U.S. mainland</a>. According to a 2015 census report,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> the county had a population of 2,693,117,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QF_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-QF-2">[2]</a></sup> making it the most populous county in Florida and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_most_populous_counties_in_the_United_States" title="List of the most populous counties in the United States">seventh-most populous county in the United States</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> It is also Florida's third-largest county in terms of land area, with 1,946 square miles (5,040 km<sup>2</sup>). The <a href="/wiki/County_seat" title="County seat">county seat</a> is <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">Miami</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GR6_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-GR6-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>Miami-Dade County is included in the <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">Miami</a>-<a href="/wiki/Fort_Lauderdale,_Florida" title="Fort Lauderdale, Florida">Fort Lauderdale</a>-<a href="/wiki/West_Palm_Beach,_Florida" title="West Palm Beach, Florida">West Palm Beach</a>, FL <a href="/wiki/Miami_metropolitan_area" title="Miami metropolitan area">Metropolitan Statistical Area</a>.</p>
<p>The county is home to 34 incorporated <a href="/wiki/City" title="City">cities</a> and many <a href="/wiki/Unincorporated_area" title="Unincorporated area">unincorporated areas</a>. The northern, central and eastern portions of the county are heavily <a href="/wiki/Urbanization" title="Urbanization">urbanized</a> with many <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High_rise" title="High rise">high rises</a> up the coastline, as well as the location of <a href="/wiki/South_Florida" title="South Florida">South Florida</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Central_business_district" title="Central business district">central business district</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Downtown_Miami" title="Downtown Miami">Downtown Miami</a>. Southern Miami-Dade County includes the <a href="/wiki/Redland,_Florida" title="Redland, Florida">Redland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Homestead,_Florida" title="Homestead, Florida">Homestead</a> areas, which make up the agricultural economy of Miami. Agricultural Redland makes up roughly one third of Miami-Dade County's inhabited land area, and is sparsely populated, a stark contrast to the densely populated, urban northern Miami-Dade County. The western portion of the county extends into the <a href="/wiki/Everglades_National_Park" title="Everglades National Park">Everglades National Park</a> and is populated only by a <a href="/wiki/Miccosukee" title="Miccosukee">Miccosukee</a> tribal village. East of the mainland in <a href="/wiki/Biscayne_Bay" title="Biscayne Bay">Biscayne Bay</a> is also <a href="/wiki/Biscayne_National_Park" title="Biscayne National Park">Biscayne National Park</a> and the <a class="external text" href="http://www.dep.state.fl.us/coastal/sites/biscayne/" rel="nofollow">Biscayne Bay Aquatic Preserves</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miami-Dade_County,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_Miami,_Florida" title="History of Miami, Florida">History of Miami, Florida</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Native_peoples">Native peoples</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miami-Dade_County,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Native peoples">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The earliest evidence of <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">Native American</a> settlement in the Miami region came from about 12,000 years ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> The first inhabitants settled on the banks of the <a href="/wiki/Miami_River_(Florida)" title="Miami River (Florida)">Miami River</a>, with the main villages on the northern banks.</p>
<p>The inhabitants at the time of first European contact were the <a href="/wiki/Tequesta" title="Tequesta">Tequesta</a> people, who controlled much of southeastern Florida, including what is now <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Miami-Dade_County" title="Miami-Dade County">Miami-Dade County</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Broward_County" title="Broward County">Broward County</a>, and the southern part of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palm_Beach_County" title="Palm Beach County">Palm Beach County</a>. The Tequesta Indians fished, hunted, and gathered the fruit and roots of plants for food, but did not practice any form of agriculture. They buried the small bones of the deceased with the rest of the body, and put the larger bones in a box for the village people to see. The Tequesta are credited with making the <a href="/wiki/Miami_Circle" title="Miami Circle">Miami Circle</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_explorers_and_settlers">European explorers and settlers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miami-Dade_County,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: European explorers and settlers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Juan_Ponce_de_Le%C3%B3n" title="Juan Ponce de León">Juan Ponce de León</a> was the first European to visit the area in 1513 by sailing into <a href="/wiki/Biscayne_Bay" title="Biscayne Bay">Biscayne Bay</a>. His journal records that he reached <i>Chequescha</i>, a varianth of <i>Tequesta</i>, which was Miami's first recorded name.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> It is unknown whether he came ashore or made contact with the natives. <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Men%C3%A9ndez_de_Avil%C3%A9s" title="Pedro Menéndez de Avilés">Pedro Menéndez de Avilés</a> and his men made the first recorded landing when they visited the <a href="/wiki/Tequesta" title="Tequesta">Tequesta</a> settlement in 1566 while looking for Avilés' missing son, shipwrecked a year earlier.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> Spanish soldiers led by Father Francisco Villarreal built a Jesuit mission at the mouth of the Miami River a year later but it was short-lived. After the Spaniards left, the Tequesta Indians were left to fend themselves from European-introduced diseases like <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">smallpox</a>. By 1711, the Tequesta sent a couple of local chiefs to <a href="/wiki/Havana" title="Havana">Havana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, to ask if they could migrate there. The Cubans sent two ships to help them, but Spanish illnesses struck and most of the Indians died.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>The first permanent European settlers arrived in the early 19th century. People came from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bahamas" title="Bahamas">Bahamas</a> to South Florida and the <a href="/wiki/Florida_Keys" title="Florida Keys">Keys</a> to hunt for treasure from the ships that ran aground on the treacherous Great <a href="/wiki/Florida_Reef" title="Florida Reef">Florida Reef</a>. Some accepted Spanish land offers along the Miami River. At about the same time, the <a href="/wiki/Seminole" title="Seminole">Seminole</a> Indians arrived, along with a group of runaway slaves. The area was affected by the <a href="/wiki/Second_Seminole_War" title="Second Seminole War">Second Seminole War</a>, during which Major <a href="/wiki/William_S._Harney" title="William S. Harney">William S. Harney</a> led several raids against the Indians. Most non-Indian residents were soldiers stationed at <a href="/wiki/Fort_Dallas" title="Fort Dallas">Fort Dallas</a>. It was the most devastating Indian war in American history, causing almost a total loss of population in Miami.</p>
<p>After the Second Seminole War ended in 1842, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=William_English_(planter)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="William English (planter) (page does not exist)">William English</a>, re-established a plantation started by his uncle on the Miami River. He charted the “Village of Miami” on the south bank of the Miami River and sold several plots of land. In 1844, Miami became the county seat, and six years later a census reported that there were ninety-six residents living in the area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Seminole_Wars#Third_Seminole_War" title="Seminole Wars">Third Seminole War</a> was not as destructive as the second one. Even so, it slowed down the settlement of southeast Florida. At the end of the war, a few of the soldiers stayed.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Birth_of_Dade_County">Birth of Dade County</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miami-Dade_County,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Birth of Dade County">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Julia_DeForest_Tuttle.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="782" data-file-width="600" height="196" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Julia_DeForest_Tuttle.jpg/150px-Julia_DeForest_Tuttle.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Julia_DeForest_Tuttle.jpg/225px-Julia_DeForest_Tuttle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Julia_DeForest_Tuttle.jpg/300px-Julia_DeForest_Tuttle.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Julia_DeForest_Tuttle.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Julia_Tuttle" title="Julia Tuttle">Julia Tuttle</a> (1849-1898), the founder of Miami.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flaglerstreet_Miami_1945.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="445" data-file-width="600" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Flaglerstreet_Miami_1945.jpg/200px-Flaglerstreet_Miami_1945.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Flaglerstreet_Miami_1945.jpg/300px-Flaglerstreet_Miami_1945.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Flaglerstreet_Miami_1945.jpg/400px-Flaglerstreet_Miami_1945.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flaglerstreet_Miami_1945.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Crowds on <a href="/wiki/Flagler_Street" title="Flagler Street">Flagler Street</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Downtown_Miami" title="Downtown Miami">Downtown</a> <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">Miami</a> on August 15, 1945, 20 minutes after the announcement of <a href="/wiki/Victory_over_Japan_Day#Public_celebrations" title="Victory over Japan Day">Japan's surrender</a> at the end of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Dade County was created on January 18, 1836, under the Territorial Act of the United States. The county was named after Major <a href="/wiki/Francis_L._Dade" title="Francis L. Dade">Francis L. Dade</a>, a soldier killed in 1835 in the <a href="/wiki/Second_Seminole_War" title="Second Seminole War">Second Seminole War</a>, at what has since been named the <a href="/wiki/Dade_Battlefield_Historic_State_Park" title="Dade Battlefield Historic State Park">Dade Battlefield</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> At the time of its creation, Dade County included the land that now contains <a href="/wiki/Palm_Beach_County,_Florida" title="Palm Beach County, Florida">Palm Beach</a> and <a href="/wiki/Broward_County,_Florida" title="Broward County, Florida">Broward</a> counties, together with the <a href="/wiki/Florida_Keys" title="Florida Keys">Florida Keys</a> from <a href="/wiki/Bahia_Honda_Key" title="Bahia Honda Key">Bahia Honda Key</a> north and the land of present-day Miami-Dade County. The county seat was originally at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indian_Key" title="Indian Key">Indian Key</a> in the Florida Keys; then in 1844, the County seat was moved to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Miami,_Florida" title="Miami, Florida">Miami</a>. The Florida Keys from <a href="/wiki/Key_Largo" title="Key Largo">Key Largo</a> to Bahia Honda were returned to <a href="/wiki/Monroe_County,_Florida" title="Monroe County, Florida">Monroe County</a> in 1866. In 1888 the county seat was moved to Juno, near present-day <a href="/wiki/Juno_Beach,_Florida" title="Juno Beach, Florida">Juno Beach, Florida</a>, returning to Miami in 1899. In 1909, Palm Beach County was formed from the northern portion of what was then Dade County, and then in 1915, Palm Beach County and Dade County contributed nearly equal portions of land to create what is now Broward County. There have been no significant boundary changes to the county since 1915.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricanes">Hurricanes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miami-Dade_County,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Hurricanes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The third-costliest <a href="/wiki/Natural_disaster" title="Natural disaster">natural disaster</a> to occur in the United States was <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Andrew" title="Hurricane Andrew">Hurricane Andrew</a>, which hit Miami early Monday morning on August 24, 1992. It struck the southern part of the county from due east, south of Miami and very near <a href="/wiki/Homestead,_Florida" title="Homestead, Florida">Homestead</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kendall,_Florida" title="Kendall, Florida">Kendall</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cutler_Ridge" title="Cutler Ridge">Cutler Ridge</a> (now the Town of <a href="/wiki/Cutler_Bay,_Florida" title="Cutler Bay, Florida">Cutler Bay</a>). Damages numbered over US$25 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1000000000_(number)" title="1000000000 (number)">billion</a> in the county alone, and recovery has taken years in these areas where the destruction was greatest. This was the costliest natural disaster in US history until <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">Hurricane Katrina</a> struck the Gulf region in 2005.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Name_change">Name change</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miami-Dade_County,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Name change">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On November 13, 1997, voters changed the name of the county from <i>Dade</i> to <i>Miami-Dade</i> to acknowledge the international name recognition of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Miami,_Florida" title="Miami, Florida">Miami</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> Voters were acting pursuant to <a href="/wiki/Home_rule" title="Home rule">home rule</a> powers granted to Dade County, including the ability to change the name of the county without the consent of the <a href="/wiki/Florida_Legislature" title="Florida Legislature">Florida Legislature</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> The change in name also addressed a source of public dissatisfaction with the name "Dade" which was chosen to honor of <a href="/wiki/Francis_L._Dade" title="Francis L. Dade">Francis L. Dade</a>, who had been killed in the <a href="/wiki/Dade_Massacre" title="Dade Massacre">Dade Massacre</a> in the 1830s. The <a href="/wiki/Dade_Massacre" title="Dade Massacre">Dade Massacre</a> did not occur in <a href="/wiki/South_Florida" title="South Florida">South Florida</a>, but in the west central part of the state, in present-day <a href="/wiki/Sumter_County,_Florida" title="Sumter County, Florida">Sumter County</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Bushnell,_Florida" title="Bushnell, Florida">Bushnell</a>. There is also a <a href="/wiki/Dade_City,_Florida" title="Dade City, Florida">Dade City</a>, which is closer to the site of the massacre.</p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; width:99%; max-width:908px;">
<div class="thumbinner" style="">
<div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Downtown_Miami_Panorama_from_the_Rusty_Pelican_photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg" title="The Miami skyline"><img alt="" data-file-height="2390" data-file-width="8972" height="240" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Downtown_Miami_Panorama_from_the_Rusty_Pelican_photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg/900px-Downtown_Miami_Panorama_from_the_Rusty_Pelican_photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Downtown_Miami_Panorama_from_the_Rusty_Pelican_photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg/1350px-Downtown_Miami_Panorama_from_the_Rusty_Pelican_photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Downtown_Miami_Panorama_from_the_Rusty_Pelican_photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg/1800px-Downtown_Miami_Panorama_from_the_Rusty_Pelican_photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg 2x" width="900"/></a></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miami-Dade_County,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Miami_Riverwalk.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Miami_Riverwalk.jpg/200px-Miami_Riverwalk.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Miami_Riverwalk.jpg/300px-Miami_Riverwalk.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Miami_Riverwalk.jpg/400px-Miami_Riverwalk.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Miami_Riverwalk.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Miami_River_(Florida)" title="Miami River (Florida)">Miami River</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Downtown_Miami" title="Downtown Miami">Downtown Miami</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Physical_geography">Physical geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miami-Dade_County,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Physical geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Census_Bureau" title="U.S. Census Bureau">U.S. Census Bureau</a>, the county has a total area of 2,431 square miles (6,300 km<sup>2</sup>), of which 1,898 square miles (4,920 km<sup>2</sup>) is land and 533 square miles (1,380 km<sup>2</sup>) (21.9%) is water.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GR1_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-GR1-18">[18]</a></sup> It is the third-largest county in Florida by land area and second-largest by total area. Most of the water is in the <a href="/wiki/Biscayne_Bay" title="Biscayne Bay">Biscayne Bay</a>, with another significant portion in the adjacent waters of the Atlantic Ocean.</p>
<p>Miami-Dade County is only about 6 feet (1.8 m) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" title="Above mean sea level">above sea level</a>. It is rather new geologically and located at the eastern edge of the <a href="/wiki/Florida_Platform" title="Florida Platform">Florida Platform</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Carbonate" title="Carbonate">carbonate</a> plateau created millions of years ago. Eastern Dade is composed of <a href="/wiki/Oolite" title="Oolite">Oolite</a> <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestone</a> while western Dade is composed mostly of <a href="/wiki/Bryozoa" title="Bryozoa">Bryozoa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> Miami-Dade is among the last areas of Florida to be created and populated with fauna and flora, mostly in the <a href="/wiki/Pleistocene" title="Pleistocene">Pleistocene</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Headlands_and_bays" title="Headlands and bays">bay</a> is divided from the Atlantic Ocean by the many barrier isles along the coast, one of which is where well-known <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Miami_Beach" title="Miami Beach">Miami Beach</a> is located, home to <a href="/wiki/South_Beach" title="South Beach">South Beach</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Art_Deco" title="Art Deco">Art Deco</a> district. The <a href="/wiki/Florida_Keys" title="Florida Keys">Florida Keys</a>, which are also barrier islands are only accessible through Miami-Dade County, but which are otherwise part of neighboring <a href="/wiki/Monroe_County,_Florida" title="Monroe County, Florida">Monroe County</a>. Miami is situated seventy miles from West Palm Beach, and thirty miles from Fort Lauderdale.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Adjacent_counties">Adjacent counties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miami-Dade_County,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Adjacent counties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Broward_County,_Florida" title="Broward County, Florida">Broward County</a> – north</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Monroe_County,_Florida" title="Monroe County, Florida">Monroe County</a> – south and west</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Collier_County,_Florida" title="Collier County, Florida">Collier County</a> – northwest</li>
</ul>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2010_U.S._Census">2010 U.S. Census</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miami-Dade_County,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: 2010 U.S. Census">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Downtown_Miami_from_north_20080408.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Downtown_Miami_from_north_20080408.jpg/200px-Downtown_Miami_from_north_20080408.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Downtown_Miami_from_north_20080408.jpg/300px-Downtown_Miami_from_north_20080408.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Downtown_Miami_from_north_20080408.jpg/400px-Downtown_Miami_from_north_20080408.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Downtown_Miami_from_north_20080408.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Since late 2001, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Downtown_Miami" title="Downtown Miami">Downtown Miami</a> has seen a large construction boom in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Skyscrapers" title="Skyscrapers">skyscrapers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Retail" title="Retail">retail</a> and has experienced <a href="/wiki/Gentrification" title="Gentrification">gentrification</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>.</div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Brickell_north_entrance.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2560" data-file-width="1920" height="267" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Brickell_north_entrance.jpg/200px-Brickell_north_entrance.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Brickell_north_entrance.jpg/300px-Brickell_north_entrance.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Brickell_north_entrance.jpg/400px-Brickell_north_entrance.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Brickell_north_entrance.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Miami's <a href="/wiki/Brickell" title="Brickell">Brickell</a> neighborhood, is amongst the fastest-growing areas of Miami-Dade County<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></div>

<p><u>U.S. Census Bureau 2010 Ethnic/Race Demographics:</u><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MiDaDemo_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-MiDaDemo-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MDD_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-MDD-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_(U.S._Census)" title="White (U.S. Census)">White (non-Hispanic)</a>: 15.4% <small>(2.3% German, 2.2% Italian, 1.8% Irish, 1.5% English, 1.0% Russian, 0.9% Polish, 0.9% French) (White total 73.8% when including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_Hispanic" title="White Hispanic">White Hispanics</a>)</small><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MiDaDemo_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-MiDaDemo-25">[25]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_(U.S._Census)" title="Black (U.S. Census)">Black (non-Hispanic)</a>: 17.1% <small>(6.9% <a href="/wiki/West_Indian" title="West Indian">West Indian</a>/<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Afro-Caribbean_American" title="Afro-Caribbean American">Afro-Caribbean American</a> [4.5% Haitian, 1.4% Jamaican, 0.3% Bahamian, 0.2% Trinidadian and Tobagonian, 0.1% <a href="/wiki/Afro-Caribbean" title="Afro-Caribbean">Other or Unspecified West Indian</a>, 0.1% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_West_Indian" title="British West Indian">British West Indian</a>,] 0.5% <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Subsaharan African</a>) (Black total 18.9% when including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_Hispanic" title="Black Hispanic">Black Hispanics</a>)</small><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hispanic_(U.S._Census)" title="Hispanic (U.S. Census)">Hispanic</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latino_(U.S._Census)" title="Latino (U.S. Census)">Latino</a> of any race: 65.0% <small>(34.3% Cuban, 4.6% Colombian, 4.2% Nicaraguan, 3.7% Puerto Rican, 2.3% Dominican, 2.2% Honduran, 2.1% Mexican, 1.9% Venezuelan, 1.6% Peruvian, 1.1% Argentinean, 0.8% Ecuadorian, 0.8% Guatemalan, 0.7% Salvadoran, 0.5% Spaniard, 0.5% Chilean)</small><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MDD_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-MDD-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_(U.S._Census)" title="Asian (U.S. Census)">Asian</a>: 1.5% <small>(0.4% Chinese, 0.4% Indian, 0.2% Filipino, 0.2% Other Asian, 0.1% Vietnamese, 0.1% Korean, 0.1% Japanese)</small><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MiDaDemo_25-2"><a href="#cite_note-MiDaDemo-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MDD_26-2"><a href="#cite_note-MDD-26">[26]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multiracial_American" title="Multiracial American">Two or more races</a>: 2.4%</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Native_American_(U.S._Census)" title="Native American (U.S. Census)">American Indian and Alaska Native</a>: 0.2%</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific_Islander_(U.S._Census)" title="Pacific Islander (U.S. Census)">Native Hawaiian and Other Pacific Islander</a>: 0.03%<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MiDaDemo_25-3"><a href="#cite_note-MiDaDemo-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MDD_26-3"><a href="#cite_note-MDD-26">[26]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census)" title="Race (United States Census)">Other Races</a>: 3.2% <small>(0.6% Arab)</small><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MiDaDemo_25-4"><a href="#cite_note-MiDaDemo-25">[25]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>In 2010, 3.4% of the Miami-Dade's population considered themselves to be of only "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_people" title="American people">American</a>" ancestry (regardless of race or ethnicity.)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MiDaDemo_25-5"><a href="#cite_note-MiDaDemo-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2010, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuban_people" title="Cuban people">Cubans</a> made up the largest population of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Immigrant" title="Immigrant">immigrants</a> (with more than half of the population,) with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colombian_people" title="Colombian people">Colombians</a> coming in second, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haitian_people" title="Haitian people">Haitians</a> in third, followed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Honduran_people" title="Honduran people">Hondurans</a> in fourth place, then <a href="/wiki/People_of_the_Dominican_Republic" title="People of the Dominican Republic">Dominicans</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Venezuelan_people" title="Venezuelan people">Venezuelans</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peruvian_people" title="Peruvian people">Peruvians</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jamaican_people" title="Jamaican people">Jamaicans</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mexican_people" title="Mexican people">Mexicans</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Argentinian_people" title="Argentinian people">Argentinians</a> among the highest group of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Expatriates" title="Expatriates">expatriates</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>There were 867,352 households out of which 30.61% had children under the age of 18 living with them, 43.8% were <a href="/wiki/Marriage" title="Marriage">married couples</a> living together, 18.79% had a female householder with no husband present, and 30.49% were non-families. 23.55% of all households were made up of individuals and 8.38% (2.52% male and 5.86% female) had someone living alone who was 65 years of age or older. The average household size was 2.83 and the average family size was 3.33.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MDD_26-4"><a href="#cite_note-MDD-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MDage_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-MDage-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>The age distribution is 21.9% under the age of 18, 9.9% from 18 to 24, 28.6% from 25 to 44, 25.6% from 45 to 64, and 14.1% who were 65 years of age or older. The median age was 38.2 years. For every 100 females there were 93.8 males. For every 100 females age 18 and over, there were 91.0 males.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MDage_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-MDage-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>The median income for a household in the county was $43,605, and the median income for a family was $50,065. Males had a median income of $35,096 versus $29,980 for females. The <a href="/wiki/Per_capita_income" title="Per capita income">per capita income</a> for the county was $22,957. About 13.8% of families and 17.2% of the population were below the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Poverty_line" title="Poverty line">poverty line</a>, including 22.0% of those under age 18 and 22.1% of those aged 65 or over.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2010, 51.1% of the county's population was <a href="/wiki/Foreign_born" title="Foreign born">foreign born</a>, with 48.7% being <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Naturalized_citizen_of_the_United_States" title="Naturalized citizen of the United States">naturalized American citizens</a>. Of foreign-born residents, 93.0% were born in <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>, 3.2% were born in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>, 2.7% born in <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>, 0.5% born in <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>, 0.5% in <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>, and 0.1% were born in <a href="/wiki/Oceania" title="Oceania">Oceania</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MiDaDemo_25-6"><a href="#cite_note-MiDaDemo-25">[25]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2000_U.S._Census">2000 U.S. Census</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miami-Dade_County,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: 2000 U.S. Census">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As of the <a href="/wiki/Census" title="Census">census</a> of 2000, there were 2,253,362 people, 776,774 households, and 548,402 families residing in the county, with an average <a href="/wiki/Population_density" title="Population density">population density</a> of 1,158 inhabitants per square mile (447/km<sup>2</sup>). There were 852,278 housing units with an average density of 438 per square mile (169/km<sup>2</sup>). The racial makeup of the county was 69.7% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census)" title="Race (United States Census)">White</a> (49% White Hispanic, 20.7% Non-Hispanic White),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> 20.3% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census)" title="Race (United States Census)">African American</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census)" title="Race (United States Census)">Black</a> (with a large part being of <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> descent), 0.20% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census)" title="Race (United States Census)">Native American</a>, 1.4% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census)" title="Race (United States Census)">Asian</a>, 0.01% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census)" title="Race (United States Census)">Pacific Islander</a>, 4.60% from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census)" title="Race (United States Census)">other races</a>, and 3.80% from two or more races. 57.3% of the population were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census)" title="Race (United States Census)">Hispanic</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census)" title="Race (United States Census)">Latino</a> of any race. In relation to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancestry" title="Ancestry">ancestry</a> (excluding the various <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census)" title="Race (United States Census)">Hispanic</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census)" title="Race (United States Census)">Latino</a> ancestries), 5% were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haitian_people" title="Haitian people">Haitian</a>, 5% American, 2% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_people" title="Italian people">Italian</a>, 2% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jamaican_people" title="Jamaican people">Jamaican</a>, 2% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_people" title="German people">German</a>, 2% <a href="/wiki/Irish_people" title="Irish people">Irish</a>, and 2% <a href="/wiki/English_people" title="English people">English</a> ancestry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-city-data_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-city-data-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>1,147,765 Miami-Dade residents—50.9% of the total population—were foreign-born, a percentage greater than that of any other <a href="/wiki/County_(United_States)" title="County (United States)">county</a> in the United States. 47% of the foreign-born population were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Naturalized#In_the_United_States" title="Naturalized">naturalized U.S. citizens</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-city-data_35-1"><a href="#cite_note-city-data-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Among the foreign-born population, the most common countries of origin were <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> (46%), <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">Nicaragua</a> (8%), <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a> (7%), <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a> (6%), the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a> (3%), <a href="/wiki/Honduras" title="Honduras">Honduras</a> (3%), <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a> (3%) and <a href="/wiki/El_Salvador" title="El Salvador">El Salvador</a> (2%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-city-data_35-2"><a href="#cite_note-city-data-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>There were 776,774 households out of which 33.8% had children under the age of 18 living with them, 47.7% were <a href="/wiki/Marriage" title="Marriage">married couples</a> living together, 17.2% had a female householder with no husband present, and 29.4% were non-families. 23.3% of all households were made up of individuals and 8.6% had someone living alone who was 65 years of age or older. The average household size was 2.84 and the average family size was 3.35.</p>
<p>The age distribution is 24.8% under the age of 18, 9.1% from 18 to 24, 31.0% from 25 to 44, 21.7% from 45 to 64, and 13.3% who were 65 years of age or older. The median age was 36 years. For every 100 females there were 93.5 males. For every 100 females age 18 and over, there were 90.2 males.</p>
<p>The median income for a household in the county was $35,966, and the median income for a family was $40,260. Males had a median income of $30,120 versus $24,686 for females. The <a href="/wiki/Per_capita_income" title="Per capita income">per capita income</a> for the county was $18,497. About 14.5% of families and 18.0% of the population were below the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Poverty_line" title="Poverty line">poverty line</a>, including 22.9% of those under age 18 and 18.9% of those age 65 or over.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miami-Dade_County,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As of 2010, 63.77% of the population spoke Spanish, 28.07% English, 4.22% <a href="/wiki/French-based_creole_languages" title="French-based creole languages">French Creole</a> (mainly <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Creole" title="Haitian Creole">Haitian Creole</a>,) 0.64% French, and 0.55% spoke Portuguese as their <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mother_language" title="Mother language">mother language</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MLA_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-MLA-37">[37]</a></sup> 52% of the county <a href="/wiki/Residency_(domicile)" title="Residency (domicile)">residents</a> were born outside the United States, while 71.93% of the <a href="/wiki/Population" title="Population">population</a> spoke a language other than English as their <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Primary_language" title="Primary language">primary language</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MLA_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-MLA-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the 1950s about 80% of the county population were English-speaking non-Hispanic whites. As of 2010 58.5% of the population natively spoke Spanish, with about half of them having <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/English_as_a_second_language" title="English as a second language">low English fluency</a>. 27.2% of the population spoke only English.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miami-Dade_County,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">

<p><a href="/wiki/Brightstar_Corporation" title="Brightstar Corporation">Brightstar Corporation</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Burger_King" title="Burger King">Burger King</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Intradeco_Holdings&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Intradeco Holdings (page does not exist)">Intradeco Holdings</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Latin_Flavors" title="Latin Flavors">Latin Flavors</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Cruise_Line" title="Norwegian Cruise Line">Norwegian Cruise Line</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Ryder" title="Ryder">Ryder</a> have their headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Unincorporated_area" title="Unincorporated area">unincorporated areas</a> in the county.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Centurion_Air_Cargo" title="Centurion Air Cargo">Centurion Air Cargo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florida_West_International_Airways" title="Florida West International Airways">Florida West International Airways</a>, <a href="/wiki/IBC_Airways" title="IBC Airways">IBC Airways</a>, and <a href="/wiki/World_Atlantic_Airlines" title="World Atlantic Airlines">World Atlantic Airlines</a> have their headquarters on the grounds of <a href="/wiki/Miami_International_Airport" title="Miami International Airport">Miami International Airport</a> in an unincorporated area in the county.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hewlett_Packard" title="Hewlett Packard">Hewlett Packard</a>'s main Latin America offices are located on the ninth floor of the Waterford Building in unincorporated Miami-Dade County.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>Other companies with offices in an unincorporated area not in any CDP:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/AstraZeneca" title="AstraZeneca">AstraZeneca</a>'s Latin American headquarters<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gate_Group" title="Gate Group">Gate Group</a>'s Latin American headquarters<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Unicomer_Group" title="Unicomer Group">Unicomer Group</a>'s United States offices<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/TAME" title="TAME">TAME</a>'s United States offices<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Goya_Foods" title="Goya Foods">Goya Foods</a>'s Miami office<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>Several defunct airlines, including <a href="/wiki/Airlift_International" title="Airlift International">Airlift International</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arrow_Air" title="Arrow Air">Arrow Air</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Airlines_(NA)" title="National Airlines (NA)">National Airlines</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rich_International_Airways" title="Rich International Airways">Rich International Airways</a>, were headquartered on or near the airport property.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p>After Frank Borman became president of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Airlines" title="Eastern Airlines">Eastern Airlines</a> in 1975, he moved Eastern's headquarters from <a href="/wiki/Rockefeller_Center" title="Rockefeller Center">Rockefeller Center</a> in <a href="/wiki/Midtown_Manhattan" title="Midtown Manhattan">Midtown Manhattan</a>, New York City to an unincorporated area in Miami-Dade County<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> Around 1991 the Miami-Dade County lost a few corporations, including Eastern Airlines, which folded in 1991.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p>At one time the cruise line <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_World_(ship)" title="The World (ship)">ResidenSea</a> had its headquarters in an unincorporated area in the county.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>

<p>Miami-Dade County includes 34 incorporated areas, 38 <a href="/wiki/Census-designated_place" title="Census-designated place">census-designated places</a>, and 16 <a href="/wiki/Unincorporated_area" title="Unincorporated area">unincorporated</a> regions.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_and_government">Law and government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miami-Dade_County,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Law and government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Miami-Dade_County" title="Government of Miami-Dade County">Government of Miami-Dade County</a></div>
<p>Miami-Dade County has operated under a unique metropolitan system of government, a "two-tier <a href="/wiki/Federation" title="Federation">federation</a>," since 1957. This was made possible when <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a> voters approved a constitutional amendment in 1956 that allowed the people of Dade County (as it was known then) to enact a <a href="/wiki/Home_rule" title="Home rule">home rule</a> <a href="/wiki/Charter" title="Charter">charter</a>. Prior to this year, home rule did not exist in Florida, and all counties were limited to the same set of powers by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Florida_Constitution" title="Florida Constitution">Florida Constitution</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_law" title="State law">state law</a>. <a href="/wiki/Mattie_Belle_Davis" title="Mattie Belle Davis">Mattie Belle Davis</a>, the first woman from Florida elected to the <a href="/wiki/American_Bar_Foundation" title="American Bar Foundation">American Bar Foundation</a> and the second woman to be elected in the US, was the first woman judge of Metropolitan Court of Dade County, Florida.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Division_between_county_and_municipality_politics">Division between county and municipality politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miami-Dade_County,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Division between county and municipality politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<p>Unlike a <a href="/wiki/Consolidated_city-county" title="Consolidated city-county">consolidated city-county</a>, where the city and county governments merge into a single entity, these two entities remain separate. Instead there are two "tiers", or levels, of government: city and county. There are 34 <a href="/wiki/Municipality" title="Municipality">municipalities</a> in the county, the City of <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">Miami</a> being the largest.</p>

<p>Cities are the "lower tier" of local government, providing police and fire protection, zoning and code enforcement, and other typical city services within their jurisdiction. These services are paid for by city taxes. The County is the "upper tier", and it provides services of a metropolitan nature, such as emergency management, airport and seaport operations, public housing and health care services, transportation, environmental services, solid waste disposal etc. These are funded by county taxes, which are assessed on all incorporated and unincorporated areas.</p>
<p>Of the county's 2.6 million total residents (as of 2013), approximately 52% live in unincorporated areas, the majority of which are heavily suburbanized. These residents are part of the Unincorporated Municipal Services Area (UMSA). For these residents, the County fills the role of both lower- and upper-tier government, the County Commission acting as their lower-tier municipal representative body. Residents within UMSA pay a UMSA tax, equivalent to a city tax, which is used to provide County residents with equivalent city services (police, fire, zoning, water and sewer, etc.). Residents of incorporated areas do not pay UMSA tax.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Structure_of_county_government">Structure of county government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miami-Dade_County,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Structure of county government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dadecountycourthouse.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2560" data-file-width="1920" height="267" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Dadecountycourthouse.jpg/200px-Dadecountycourthouse.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Dadecountycourthouse.jpg/300px-Dadecountycourthouse.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Dadecountycourthouse.jpg/400px-Dadecountycourthouse.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dadecountycourthouse.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Miami-Dade_County_Courthouse" title="Miami-Dade County Courthouse">Dade County Courthouse</a>, completed in 1926</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_mayors_of_Miami-Dade_County,_Florida" title="List of mayors of Miami-Dade County, Florida">List of mayors of Miami-Dade County, Florida</a></div>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mayor_of_Miami-Dade_County" title="Mayor of Miami-Dade County">Mayor of Miami-Dade County</a> is elected countywide to serve a four-year term and is considered a "strong mayor." The mayor is not a member of the County Commission, appoints all 25 directors who oversee the operations of the County Departments and has <a href="/wiki/Veto" title="Veto">veto</a> power over the Commission. A mayoral appointment and veto can only be overridden by a two-thirds majority of the County Commission. The post is occupied by <a href="/wiki/Carlos_A._Gim%C3%A9nez" title="Carlos A. Giménez">Carlos A. Giménez</a>.</p>
<p>The Board of County Commissioners is the legislative body, consisting of 13 members elected from single-member districts. Members are elected to serve four-year terms, and elections of members are staggered. The Board chooses a Chairperson, who presides over the Commission, as well as appoints the members of its legislative committees. The Board has a wide array of powers to enact legislation, create departments, and regulate businesses operating within the County. It also has the power to override the Mayor's veto with a two-thirds vote.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a>'s <a href="/wiki/State_constitution_(United_States)" title="State constitution (United States)">Constitution</a> provides for six elected officials to oversee executive and administrative functions for each county (called "Constitutional Officers"): <a href="/wiki/Sheriff" title="Sheriff">Sheriff</a>, Property Appraiser, Supervisor of Elections, Tax Collector, Clerk of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Circuit_Court" title="Circuit Court">Circuit Court</a> and Comptroller. However, the current Constitution allows voters in home-rule counties (including Miami-Dade) to abolish the offices and reorganize them as subordinate County departments; Miami-Dade voters chose this option for Sheriff, Supervisor of Elections, Controller and Tax Collector. The office of Clerk of the Circuit Court, and the judicial offices of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_Attorney" title="State Attorney">State Attorney</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_Defender" title="Public Defender">Public Defender</a>, are still branches of State government and are, therefore, independently elected and not part of County government.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The most visible distinction between Miami-Dade and other Florida counties is the title of its law enforcement agency. It is the only county in Florida that does not have an elected sheriff, or an agency titled "Sheriff's Office."<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Instead, the equivalent agency is known as the Miami-Dade Police Department, and its leader is known as the Metropolitan Sheriff and Director of the Miami-Dade Police Department. However, the badges of Miami-Dade police officers still have "Deputy Sheriff, Dade County, Fla." inscribed.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_services">Public services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miami-Dade_County,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Public services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fire_Rescue">Fire Rescue</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miami-Dade_County,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Fire Rescue">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Miami-Dade_Fire_Rescue_Department" title="Miami-Dade Fire Rescue Department">Miami-Dade Fire Rescue Department</a></div>
<p>The Miami-Dade County Fire Rescue Department is the agency that provides <a href="/wiki/Fire_protection" title="Fire protection">fire protection</a> and <a href="/wiki/Emergency_medical_services" title="Emergency medical services">emergency medical services</a> for Miami-Dade County, Florida. The department serves 29 municipalities and all unincorporated areas of Miami-Dade County from 60 fire stations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> The Department also provides fire protection services for <a href="/wiki/Miami_International_Airport" title="Miami International Airport">Miami International Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miami_Executive_Airport" title="Miami Executive Airport">Miami Executive Airport</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Opa-locka_Airport" title="Opa-locka Airport">Opa-locka Airport</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>The communities served are <a href="/wiki/Aventura,_Florida" title="Aventura, Florida">Aventura</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bal_Harbour,_Florida" title="Bal Harbour, Florida">Bal Harbour</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bay_Harbor_Islands,_Florida" title="Bay Harbor Islands, Florida">Bay Harbor Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biscayne_Park,_Florida" title="Biscayne Park, Florida">Biscayne Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cutler_Bay,_Florida" title="Cutler Bay, Florida">Cutler Bay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Doral,_Florida" title="Doral, Florida">Doral</a>, <a href="/wiki/El_Portal,_Florida" title="El Portal, Florida">El Portal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florida_City,_Florida" title="Florida City, Florida">Florida City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golden_Beach,_Florida" title="Golden Beach, Florida">Golden Beach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hialeah_Gardens,_Florida" title="Hialeah Gardens, Florida">Hialeah Gardens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Homestead,_Florida" title="Homestead, Florida">Homestead</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indian_Creek,_Florida" title="Indian Creek, Florida">Indian Creek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Medley,_Florida" title="Medley, Florida">Medley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miami_Gardens,_Florida" title="Miami Gardens, Florida">Miami Gardens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miami_Lakes,_Florida" title="Miami Lakes, Florida">Miami Lakes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miami_Shores,_Florida" title="Miami Shores, Florida">Miami Shores</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miami_Springs,_Florida" title="Miami Springs, Florida">Miami Springs</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Bay_Village,_Florida" title="North Bay Village, Florida">North Bay Village</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Miami,_Florida" title="North Miami, Florida">North Miami</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Miami_Beach,_Florida" title="North Miami Beach, Florida">North Miami Beach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Opa-locka,_Florida" title="Opa-locka, Florida">Opa-locka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palmetto_Bay,_Florida" title="Palmetto Bay, Florida">Palmetto Bay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pinecrest,_Florida" title="Pinecrest, Florida">Pinecrest</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Miami,_Florida" title="South Miami, Florida">South Miami</a>, <a href="/wiki/Surfside,_Florida" title="Surfside, Florida">Surfside</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sweetwater,_Miami-Dade_County,_Florida" title="Sweetwater, Miami-Dade County, Florida">Sweetwater</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sunny_Isles_Beach,_Florida" title="Sunny Isles Beach, Florida">Sunny Isles Beach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Gardens,_Florida" title="Virginia Gardens, Florida">Virginia Gardens</a>, and <a href="/wiki/West_Miami,_Florida" title="West Miami, Florida">West Miami</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p>Miami-Dade Fire Rescue is also the home to <a href="/wiki/Urban_Search_and_Rescue_Florida_Task_Force_1" title="Urban Search and Rescue Florida Task Force 1">Urban Search and Rescue Florida Task Force 1</a> as well as EMS operations consisting of 57 Advanced Life Support units staffed by 760 state-certified paramedics and 640 state-certified emergency medical technicians.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Police_Department">Police Department</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miami-Dade_County,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Police Department">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Miami-Dade_Police_Department" title="Miami-Dade Police Department">Miami-Dade Police Department</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ford_Crown_Vic_Mdpdinterceptor.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2748" data-file-width="3664" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Ford_Crown_Vic_Mdpdinterceptor.JPG/200px-Ford_Crown_Vic_Mdpdinterceptor.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Ford_Crown_Vic_Mdpdinterceptor.JPG/300px-Ford_Crown_Vic_Mdpdinterceptor.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Ford_Crown_Vic_Mdpdinterceptor.JPG/400px-Ford_Crown_Vic_Mdpdinterceptor.JPG 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ford_Crown_Vic_Mdpdinterceptor.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A Miami-Dade <a href="/wiki/Police_car" title="Police car">police car</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Miami-Dade Police Department is a full service <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_police" title="Metropolitan police">metropolitan police department</a> serving Miami-Dade County's unincorporated areas, although they have lenient mutual aid agreements with other municipalities, most often the <a href="/wiki/Miami_Police_Department" title="Miami Police Department">City of Miami Police Department</a>. The Miami-Dade Police Department is the largest police department in the state of Florida with over 4,700 employees. The Department is still often referred by its former name, the <i>Metro-Dade Police</i> or simply <i>Metro</i>.</p>
<p>The Miami-Dade Police Department operate out of nine districts throughout Miami-Dade County and have two special bureaus. The current director of the department is Juan Perez, who succeeded J. D. Patterson, Jr.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> The Department's headquarters are located in <a href="/wiki/Doral,_Florida" title="Doral, Florida">Doral, Florida</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water_and_Sewer_Department">Water and Sewer Department</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miami-Dade_County,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Water and Sewer Department">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Miami-Dade_Water_and_Sewer_Department&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Miami-Dade Water and Sewer Department (page does not exist)">Miami-Dade Water and Sewer Department</a> (MDWASD) is one of the largest public utilities in the United States, employing approximately 2,700 employees as of 2007. It provides service to over 2.4 million customers, operating with an annual budget of almost $400 million. Approximately 330 million gallons of water are drawn everyday from the Biscayne Aquifer for consumer use. MDWASD has over 7,100 miles (11,400 km) of water lines, a service area of 396 square miles (1,026 km<sup>2</sup>) and 14 pump stations. MDWASD has over 3,600 miles (5,800 km) of sewage pipes, a service area of 341 square miles (883 km<sup>2</sup>) and 954 pump stations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Corrections_department">Corrections department</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miami-Dade_County,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Corrections department">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Miami-Dade_County_Corrections_and_Rehabilitation_Department" title="Miami-Dade County Corrections and Rehabilitation Department">Miami-Dade County Corrections and Rehabilitation Department</a> is the correction agency.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Aviation_department">Aviation department</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miami-Dade_County,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Aviation department">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Miami-Dade_Aviation_Department" title="Miami-Dade Aviation Department">Miami-Dade Aviation Department</a> operates <a href="/wiki/Miami_International_Airport" title="Miami International Airport">Miami International Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miami_Executive_Airport" title="Miami Executive Airport">Miami Executive Airport</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Opa-locka_Executive_Airport" title="Opa-locka Executive Airport">Opa-locka Executive Airport</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Homestead_General_Aviation_Airport" title="Homestead General Aviation Airport">Homestead General Aviation Airport</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dade-Collier_Training_and_Transition_Airport" title="Dade-Collier Training and Transition Airport">Dade-Collier Training and Transition Airport</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="County_representation">County representation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miami-Dade_County,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: County representation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Florida_Department_of_Juvenile_Justice" title="Florida Department of Juvenile Justice">Florida Department of Juvenile Justice</a> operates the Miami-Dade Regional Juvenile Detention Center in an <a href="/wiki/Unincorporated_area" title="Unincorporated area">unincorporated area</a> in the county.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miami-Dade_County,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:University_of_Miami_Otto_G._Richter_Library.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/University_of_Miami_Otto_G._Richter_Library.jpg/200px-University_of_Miami_Otto_G._Richter_Library.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/University_of_Miami_Otto_G._Richter_Library.jpg/300px-University_of_Miami_Otto_G._Richter_Library.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/University_of_Miami_Otto_G._Richter_Library.jpg/400px-University_of_Miami_Otto_G._Richter_Library.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:University_of_Miami_Otto_G._Richter_Library.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/University_of_Miami" title="University of Miami">University of Miami</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In Florida, each county is also a <a href="/wiki/School_district" title="School district">school district</a>. <a href="/wiki/Miami-Dade_County_Public_Schools" title="Miami-Dade County Public Schools">Miami-Dade County Public Schools</a>, is operated by an independently elected <a href="/wiki/Board_of_education" title="Board of education">School Board</a>. A professional <a href="/wiki/Superintendent_(education)" title="Superintendent (education)">Superintendent of Schools</a> manages the day-to-day operations of the district, who is appointed by and serves at the pleasure of the School Board. The <a href="/wiki/Miami-Dade_County_Public_Schools" title="Miami-Dade County Public Schools">Miami-Dade County Public School District</a> is currently the <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_largest_school_districts_in_the_United_States_by_enrollment" title="List of the largest school districts in the United States by enrollment">fourth-largest</a> public school district in the nation with almost 400,000 students in 2007/2008.</p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Miami-Dade_Public_Library" title="Miami-Dade Public Library">Miami-Dade Public Library</a> is one of the largest public library systems in the country, comprising 42 branch locations, and 8 branch locations currently being built/not officially opened.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miami-Dade_County,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transportation_in_Miami" title="Transportation in Miami">Transportation in Miami</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airports">Airports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miami-Dade_County,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Airports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Miami_International_Airport_aerial_2007.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="986" data-file-width="1346" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Miami_International_Airport_aerial_2007.jpg/220px-Miami_International_Airport_aerial_2007.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Miami_International_Airport_aerial_2007.jpg/330px-Miami_International_Airport_aerial_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Miami_International_Airport_aerial_2007.jpg/440px-Miami_International_Airport_aerial_2007.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Miami_International_Airport_aerial_2007.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Miami_International_Airport" title="Miami International Airport">Miami International Airport</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Miami_International_Airport" title="Miami International Airport">Miami International Airport</a>, located in an <a href="/wiki/Unincorporated_area" title="Unincorporated area">unincorporated area</a> in the county, serves as the primary international airport of the Miami Area. One of the busiest international airports in the world, Miami International Airport caters to over 35 million passengers a year. Identifiable locally, as well as several worldwide authorities, as MIA or KMIA, the airport is a major hub and the single largest international gateway for <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American Airlines</a>, the world’s largest passenger air carrier. Miami International is the United States’ third largest international port of entry for foreign air passengers (behind New York's <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport" title="John F. Kennedy International Airport">John F. Kennedy International Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_International_Airport" title="Los Angeles International Airport">Los Angeles International Airport</a>), and is the seventh largest such gateway in the world. The airport’s extensive international route network includes non-stop flights to over seventy international cities in North and South America, Europe, Asia, and the Middle East.</p>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Homestead_General_Aviation_Airport" title="Homestead General Aviation Airport">Homestead General Aviation Airport</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Miami_Executive_Airport" title="Miami Executive Airport">Miami Executive Airport</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Opa-Locka_Executive" title="Opa-Locka Executive">Opa-Locka Executive</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Homestead_Air_Reserve_Base" title="Homestead Air Reserve Base">Homestead Air Reserve Base</a>, east of Homestead in an unincorporated area, serves military traffic.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Miami_Seaplane_Base" title="Miami Seaplane Base">Miami Seaplane Base</a></li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Dade-Collier&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Dade-Collier (page does not exist)">Dade-Collier</a></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_transit">Public transit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miami-Dade_County,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Public transit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Government_Center_rush_hour.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1280" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Government_Center_rush_hour.png/220px-Government_Center_rush_hour.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Government_Center_rush_hour.png/330px-Government_Center_rush_hour.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Government_Center_rush_hour.png/440px-Government_Center_rush_hour.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Government_Center_rush_hour.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Government_Center_(MDT_station)" title="Government Center (MDT station)">Government Center</a>, one of the main <a href="/wiki/Metro_station" title="Metro station">metro stations</a> in <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">Miami</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Public transit in Miami-Dade County is served by <a class="external text" href="http://www.miamidade.gov/transit/" rel="nofollow">Miami-Dade Transportation and Public Works</a>, and is the largest public transit in Florida. Miami-Dade Transportation and Public Works operates a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heavy_rail" title="Heavy rail">heavy rail</a> <a href="/wiki/Rapid_transit" title="Rapid transit">metro</a> system <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metrorail_(Miami)" title="Metrorail (Miami)">Metrorail</a>, an elevated <a href="/wiki/People_mover" title="People mover">people mover</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Downtown_Miami" title="Downtown Miami">Downtown Miami</a>, <a href="/wiki/Metromover" title="Metromover">Metromover</a> and the bus system, <a href="/wiki/Miami-Dade_Transit#Metrobus" title="Miami-Dade Transit">Metrobus</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>

<p>In Florida a Tolled <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_Road" title="State Road">State Road</a> is often (but not always) denoted by having the word "TOLL" printed on the top of the State Road shield.</p>
<p>When a driver passes through a toll plaza without paying the proper toll a digital image of the car's license tag is recorded. Under Florida Law, this image can be used by the Authority to issue a toll violation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<p>Miami-Dade County has 10 major expressways and 1 minor expressway in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Downtown_Miami" title="Downtown Miami">Downtown Miami</a>.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="County_roads">County roads</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miami-Dade_County,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: County roads">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>This is a list of Miami-Dade county roads. Miami-Dade County has fewer county roads than any other county in Florida, despite its large population. None are signed.</p>
